        </div><div class="casAbstract">A series of O3-phase NaFex(Ni0.5Mn0.5)1-xO2 (x = 0, 0.1, 0.2, 0.3, 0.4, and 1) samples with different Fe contents was prepd. and investigated as high-capacity cathode materials of Na-ion batteries.  The partial substitution of Ni and Mn with Fe in the O3-phase lattice can greatly improve the electrochem. performance and the structural stability.  A NaFe0.2Mn0.4Ni0.4O2 cathode with an optimized Fe content of x = 0.2 can deliver an initial reversible capacity of 131 mA-h/g, a reversible capacity &gt;95% over 30 cycles, and a high rate capacity of 86 mA-h/g at 10C in a voltage range of 2.0-4.0 V.  The structural characterizations reveal that pristine NaMn0.5Ni0.5O2 and Fe-substituted NaFe0.2Mn0.4Ni0.4O2 lattices underwent different phase transformations from P3 to P3'' and from P3 to OP2 phases, resp., at high voltage interval.  The as-obtained OP2 phase by Fe substitution has smaller interslab distance (5.13 Å) than the P3'' phase (5.72 Å), which suppresses the co-insertion of the solvent mols., the electrolyte anions, or both and therefore enhances the cycling stability in the high voltage charge.                         cas_cit15R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">15</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Synthesis and electrochemical performance of Ni doped Na3V2(PO4)3/C cathode materials for sodium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Bao; Chen, Hezhang; Tong, Hui; Wang, Xu; Zheng, Junchao; Yu, Wanjing; Zhang, Jiafeng; Li, Jiangpeng; Zhang, Wei</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Alloys and Compounds</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">To improve the electrochem. performances of Na3V2(PO4) cathode materials in sodium ion batteries, Na3V2-xNix(PO4)3/C (x = 0, 0.01, 0.03 and 0.05) materials were designed and prepd. through a facile sol-gel route.  The effect of Ni doping on the compn. and crystal structure of Ni doped Na3V2(PO4)/C samples was investigated.  The results confirmed that Ni atoms were successfully doped into Na3V2(PO4) crystal and substituted the V sites.  It is shown that a carbon layer of about 2 nm was covered on the particle surface of the sample, which is beneficial for enhancing the electronic cond.  The discharge capacities of all Ni doped samples were improved at high rates (2, 5 and 10 C).  When Ni doping content was 3%, the sample exhibited the best rate performance and cycling capability.  Na3V1.97Ni0.03(PO4)3/C sample delivered the specific capacity of 98.1 mAh·g-1 at 5 C, which is much higher than that of pristine sample, 64.3 mAh·g-1.  The capacity retentions of Na3V1.97Ni0.03(PO4)3/C and pristine samples were 93.5% and 60.2%, after 50 cycles at 5 C, resp.  Electrochem. impedance spectroscopy and cyclic voltammetry performance analyses revealed that the polarization of the electrodes decreased and the diffusion coeff. of sodium ions increased by Ni doping.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref16"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref16" class="refNumLink">16</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit16" data-doi="10.1002/celc.201500052"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Aragón, M.                         cas_cit17R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">17</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Effects of Mg doping on the remarkably enhanced electrochemical performance of Na3V2(PO4)3 cathode materials for sodium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Hui; Yu, Xiqian; Bai, Ying; Wu, Feng; Wu, Chuan; Liu, Liang-Yu; Yang, Xiao-Qing</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Na3V2-xMgx(PO4)3/C composites with different Mg2+ doping contents (x = 0, 0.01, 0.03, 0.05, 0.07 and 0.1) were prepd. by a facile sol-gel method.  The doping effects on the crystal structure were investigated by XRD, XPS and EXAFS.  The results show that low dose doping of Mg2+ does not alter the structure of the material, and magnesium is successfully substituted for the vanadium site.  The Mg-doped Na3V2-xMgx(PO4)3/C composites exhibit significant improvements on the electrochem. performance in terms of the rate capability and cycle performance, esp. for the Na3V1.95Mg0.05(PO4)3/C.  For example, when the c.d. increased from 1 C to 30 C, the specific capacity only decreased from 112.5 to 94.2 mA h g-1 showing very good rate capability.  Moreover, even cycling at a high rate of 20 C, an excellent capacity retention of 81% is maintained from the initial value of 106.4 to 86.2 mA h g-1 at the 50th cycle.  Enhanced rate capability and cycle performance can be attributed to the optimized particle size, structural stability and enhanced ionic and electronic cond. induced by Mg doping.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref18"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref18" class="refNumLink">18</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit18" data-doi="10.1021/nl500548a"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhu, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Song, K.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">van Aken, P.                         cas_cit18R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">18</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Carbon-Coated Na3V2(PO4)3 Embedded in Porous Carbon Matrix: An Ultrafast Na-Storage Cathode with the Potential of Outperforming Li Cathodes</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhu, Changbao; Song, Kepeng; van Aken, Peter A.; Maier, Joachim; Yu, Yan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Letters</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Na ion batteries are one of the realistic promising alternatives to the Li analogs.  However, neither theor. energy/power d. nor the practical values reach the values of Li cathodes.  Poorer performance is expected owing to larger size, larger mass, and lower cell voltage.  Nonetheless, Na ion batteries are considered to be practically relevant in view of the abundance of the element Na.  The arguments in favor of Li and to the disadvantage of Na would be completely obsolete if the specific performance data of the latter would match the 1st.  Here the authors present a cathode consisting of C-coated nanosized Na3V2(PO4)3 embedded in a porous C matrix, which not only matches but even out-shines Li cathodes under high rate conditions.                         cas_cit19R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">19</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Self-sacrificed synthesis of three-dimensional Na3V2(PO4)3 nanofiber network for high-rate sodium-ion full batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Ren, Wenhao; Zheng, Zhiping; Xu, Chang; Niu, Chaojiang; Wei, Qiulong; An, Qinyou; Zhao, Kangning; Yan, Mengyu; Qin, Mingsheng; Mai, Liqiang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Energy</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The morphol. optimization of Na3V2(PO4)3 (NVP) material has a great significance for improving the electrochem. performance since NVP suffers from intrinsic low electronic cond.  For this purpose, a novel 3D NVP nanofiber network is controllably constructed via a facile self-sacrificed template method.  Based on time-dependent expts., an outside-in morphol. evolution mechanism from microsphere to 3D nanofiber network is proposed.  The as-synthesized material exhibits excellent cyclability (95.9% capacity retention over 1000 cycles at 10 C) and enhanced high-rate performance (94 mA h g-1 at 100 C) for sodium half cell.  Notably, when evaluated as full battery (NaTi2(PO4)3 as anode) cathode, it also shows outstanding cycling stability (96.9% capacity retention over 300 cycles at 5 C) and superior rate capability (80 mA h g-1 at 50 C).  Such remarkable performance is attributed to the 3D nanofiber network structure, which provides multi-channel ionic diffusion pathway, continuous electronic conduction, and improved structural integrity.  This self-sacrificed template strategy presented here can inspire new thought in constructing novel nanofiber/nanowire structures and accelerate the development of high-power sodium-ion batteries.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref20"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref20" class="refNumLink">20</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit20" data-doi="10.1039/c3nr05329f"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Tang, K.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Song, K.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">van Aken, P.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries are considered as prime alternatives to lithium-ion batteries for large-scale renewable energy storage units due to their low cost and the abundance of sodium bearing precursors in the earth's mineral deposits.  In the current work, a 3D NASICON framework Na3V2(PO4)3/carbon cathode electrode with 20-30 nm Na3V2(PO4)3 nanoparticles uniformly encapsulated interconnecting one-dimensional carbon nanofibers was fabricated using a simple and scalable electrospinning method.  The Na3V2(PO4)3/C cathode showed an initial charge capacity of 103 mA h g-1 and a discharge capacity of 101 mA h g-1 (calcd. on the total mass of Na3V2(PO4)3 and carbon) at 0.1C rate, and retained stable discharge capacities of 77, 58, 39 and 20 mA h g-1 at high current densities of 2C, 5C, 10C and 20C, resp.  Moreover, because of the efficient 1D sodium-ion transport pathway and the highly conductive network of Na3V2(PO4)3/C, the electrode exhibited high overall capacities even when cycled at high currents, extending its usability to high power applications.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref21"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref21" class="refNumLink">21</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit21" data-doi="10.1016/j.nanoen.2016.09.024"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, T.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, B.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Gu, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ling, M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, G.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, D.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhang, S.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">All-climate sodium ion batteries based on the NASICON electrode materials</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Nano Energy</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2016</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">30</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">756</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">761</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">In this work, we have achieved all-climate high-rate performance of sodium ion batteries by utilizing electrode materials with Na Super Ionic Conductor (NASICON) cryst. structure.  A designed NASICON-structured carbon-coated Na3V2(PO4)3 (NVP@C) nanocomposite exhibits an excellent performance at high rates in a wide temp. range (i.e., from -20 to 55 °C).                         cas_cit22R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">22</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Double-Nanocarbon Synergistically Modified Na3V2(PO4)3: An Advanced Cathode for High-Rate and Long-Life Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Shen, Wei; Li, Hui; Guo, Ziyang; Wang, Cong; Li, Zhihong; Xu, Qunjie; Liu, Haimei; Wang, Yonggang; Xia, Yongyao</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">An advanced cathode material, nitrogen-doped carbon-coated Na3V2(PO4)3 hybriding with multiwalled carbon nanotubes (CNTs) composite, namely double-nanocarbon synergistically modified Na3V2(PO4)3 of sodium ion battery, was fabricated through a simple sol-gel approach.  According to the systemical anal. of exptl. results on this composite structure, it is found that N-doping not only increases Na-ion migration velocity across the carbon-coated layer but also improves the elec. cond. of the carbon layer.  More importantly, the CNTs 3D conducting network could significantly accelerate the electron transport between multiple particles of Na3V2(PO4)3, due to the intimate contacts between active materials and CNTs.  Consenquently, the electrochem. properties of this double-nanocarbon-modified Na3V2(PO4)3 are significantly enhanced, esp. the high-rate capability and long cycle life.  For instance, its initial capacity of 94.5 mAh g-1 at 0.2 C decreases to 70 mAh g-1 at 70 C, and the capacity retention is 74%.         </div><div class="casAbstract">The electrochem. properties of Na3V2(PO4)3 nanograins having different carbon contents were investigated by a one-step solid state reaction and evaluated in different electrolyte systems.  It was found that the sodium storage performance in terms of capacity, coulombic efficiency and cyclability can be significantly improved in a new sodium bis(fluorosulfonyl) imide/propylene carbonate electrolyte which is introduced for the first time, bringing this material close to viability as a promising cathode for room-temp. sodium-ion batteries.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Although many routes have been developed that can efficiently improve the electrochem. performance of LiFePO4 (LFP) cathodes for Li-ion batteries, few of them meet the urgent industrial requirements of large-scale prodn., low cost and excellent performance.  In this work, using a hydrothermal synthetic process followed by high-temp. lithiation, we are able to design a porous micro-spherical LFP/carbon nanotubes (CNTs) nanocomposite.  The efficient combination of the inner CNTs and the outer carbon layer along with the porous structure of the LFP/CNT nanocomposite lead to its excellent electrochem. performance.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A hierarchical carbon framework wrapped Na3V2(PO4)3 is used as a superior high-rate and extended lifespan cathode for sodium-ion batteries.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref27"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref27" class="refNumLink">27</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit27" data-doi="10.1016/j.electacta.2015.03.091"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhang, J.-f.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, X.-w.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhang, B.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Peng, C.-l.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Tong, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yang, Z.-h.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Multicore-shell carbon-coated lithium manganese phosphate and lithium vanadium phosphate composite material with high capacity and cycling performance for lithium-ion battery</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Electrochim.                         cas_cit27R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">27</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Multicore-shell carbon-coated lithium manganese phosphate and lithium vanadium phosphate composite material with high capacity and cycling performance for lithium-ion battery</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Jia-feng; Wang, Xiao-wei; Zhang, Bao; Peng, Chun-li; Tong, Hui; Yang, Zhan-hong</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Electrochimica Acta</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">169</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">462-469</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ELCAAV</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0013-4686</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The energy crisis and energy security leads a great attention to Li-ion batteries (LIB) as the excellent power candidates.  The authors successfully synthesized LiMnPO4·Li3V2(PO4)3/C composite cathode material with high capacity and excellent cycling performance from prickly MnV2O6·2H2O precursor, following chem. redn. and lithiation with double C sources.  The LiMnPO4·Li3V2(PO4)3/C sample has a special multicore-shell structure, whose inner stuffing are LiMnPO4 and Li3V2(PO4)3 at 5-25 nm.  The initial discharge capacity of LiMnPO4·Li3V2(PO4)3/C composite delivers 221.4 mAh g-1, 202.3 mAh g-1 and 152.9 mAh g-1 at the rate of 0.1 C, 1 C and 5 C at 1.5-4.5 V, and retains 99.5%, 99.1% and 94.3% of its initial discharge capacity after 50 cycles, resp.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref28"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref28" class="refNumLink">28</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit28" data-doi="10.1016/j.jpowsour.2016.02.066"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Klee, R.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Lavela, P.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Aragon, M. J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Alcantara, R.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Tirado, J. L.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Enhanced high-rate performance of manganese substituted Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub>/C as cathode for sodium-ion batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">J. Power Sources</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2016</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">313</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">73</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">80</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1016/j.jpowsour.2016.02.066</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D313%26publication_year%3D2016%26pages%3D73-80%26journal%3DJ.%2BPower%2BSources%26author%3DR.%2BKlee%26author%3DP.%2BLavela%26author%3DM.%2BJ.%2BAragon%26author%3DR.%2BAlcantara%26author%3DJ.%2BL.%2BTirado%26title%3DEnhanced%2Bhigh-rate%2Bperformance%2Bof%2Bmanganese%2Bsubstituted%2BNa3V2%2528PO4%25293%252FC%2Bas%2Bcathode%2Bfor%2Bsodium-ion%2Bbatteries%26doi%3D10.1016%252Fj.jpowsour.2016.02.066&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.7b16402&amp;doiOfLink=10.1016%2Fj.jpowsour.2016.02.066&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit28R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">28</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Enhanced high-rate performance of manganese substituted Na3V2(PO4)3/C as cathode for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Klee, R.; Lavela, P.; Aragon, M. J.; Alcantara, R.; Tirado, J. L.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Power Sources</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">313</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">73-80</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JPSODZ</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0378-7753</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Composites with general stoichiometry Na3V2-xMnx(PO4)3/C (0 ≤ x ≤ 0.7) have been evaluated as cathode materials in sodium-ion batteries.  The sol-gel method here employed favors the formation of a homogeneously dispersed carbon conductive phase.  XRD patterns show a limited soly. of Mn in the NASICON structure.  The substitution of 0.3-0.5 manganese per formula unit promotes the formation of a homogeneous composite.  XPS spectra evidence an effective substitution of V3+ by Mn3+.  Galvanostatic cycling of sodium half-cell reveal a plateau at 3.4 V ascribable to the V4+/V3+ redox couple.  A small and reversible plateau at ca. 3.85 V is also obsd. for x ≥ 0.3, and ascribed to the activation of the V5+/V4+ redox couple, according to XPS spectroscopy.  Ex-situ XRD patterns NayV1.7Mn0.3(PO4)3 evidence the occurrence of a reversible two phase mechanism of sodium insertion.  An optimized performance is achieved for Na3V1.7Mn0.3(PO4)3/C, reaching a capacity value of 104 mA h/g at C/2 and 92 mA h/g at 2C.  It is ascribed to the optimal morphol., leading to low internal resistance and favorable electrode-electrolyte interphase.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref29"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref29" class="refNumLink">29</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit29" data-doi="10.1016/j.jpowsour.2013.03.035"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Shu, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wu, Q.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Hu, B.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yang, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wei, Q.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liang, Q.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Bai, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhou, M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wu, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chen, M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, A.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Jiang, L.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Improved electrochemical performance of LiFePO<sub>4</sub>/C cathode via Ni and Mn co-doping for lithium-ion batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">J. Power Sources</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2013</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">237</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">149</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">155</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1016/j.jpowsour.2013.03.035</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D237%26publication_year%3D2013%26pages%3D149-155%26journal%3DJ.%2BPower%2BSources%26author%3DH.%2BShu%26author%3DX.%2BWang%26author%3DQ.%2BWu%26author%3DB.%2BHu%26author%3DX.%2BYang%26author%3DQ.%2BWei%26author%3DQ.%2BLiang%26author%3DY.%2BBai%26author%3DM.%2BZhou%26author%3DC.%2BWu%26author%3DM.%2BChen%26author%3DA.%2BWang%26author%3DL.%2BJiang%26title%3DImproved%2Belectrochemical%2Bperformance%2Bof%2BLiFePO4%252FC%2Bcathode%2Bvia%2BNi%2Band%2BMn%2Bco-doping%2Bfor%2Blithium-ion%2Bbatteries%26doi%3D10.1016%252Fj.jpowsour.2013.03.035&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.7b16402&amp;doiOfLink=10.1016%2Fj.jpowsour.2013.03.035&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit29R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">29</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Improved electrochemical performance of LiFePO4/C cathode via Ni and Mn co-doping for lithium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Shu, Hongbo; Wang, Xianyou; Wu, Qiang; Hu, Benan; Yang, Xiukang; Wei, Qiliang; Liang, Qianqian; Bai, Yansong; Zhou, Meng; Wu, Chun; Chen, Manfang; Wang, Aiwen; Jiang, Lanlan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Power Sources</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2013</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">237</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">149-155</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JPSODZ</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0378-7753</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The pristine LiFePO4/C and Ni and Mn co-doped LiFe1-x-yNixMnyPO4/C (x = 0.01-0.04; y = 0.04-0.01) composites are synthesized by a simple high-temp. solid-state route.  The structure, morphol. and electrochem. performance of the samples are characterized by x-ray diffraction, FTIR spectra, SEM, charge/discharge tests and electrochem. impedance spectroscopy.  The results indicate that the Ni and Mn co-doping does not destroy the olivine structure of LiFePO4, but it can stabilize the crystal structure, lengthen the Li-O bond, decrease charge transfer resistance, enhance Li ion diffusion velocity, and thus improve the cycling and high-rate capability of the LiFePO4/C.  Esp., the LiFe0.95Ni0.02Mn0.03PO4/C shows the best cycling stability and rate capability among all the doped samples.  The first discharge capacity of LiFe0.95Ni0.02Mn0.03PO4/C is 145.4 mA-h/g with the capacity retention ratio of 98.6% for 100 cycles at 1C.  Even at a high rate of 10C, it still shows a high discharge capacity of 115.2 mA-h/g.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref30"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref30" class="refNumLink">30</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit30" data-doi="10.1016/j.electacta.2015.08.109"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhang, J.-f.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, X.-w.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhang, B.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Tong, H.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Porous spherical LiMnPO<sub>4</sub>·2Li<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub>/C cathode material synthesized via spray-drying route using oxalate complex for lithium-ion batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Electrochim. Acta</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2015</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">180</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">507</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">513</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1016/j.electacta.2015.08.109</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D180%26publication_year%3D2015%26pages%3D507-513%26journal%3DElectrochim.%2BActa%26author%3DJ.-f.%2BZhang%26author%3DX.-w.%2BWang%26author%3DB.%2BZhang%26author%3DH.%2BTong%26title%3DPorous%2Bspherical%2BLiMnPO4%25C2%25B72Li3V2%2528PO4%25293%252FC%2Bcathode%2Bmaterial%2Bsynthesized%2Bvia%2Bspray-drying%2Broute%2Busing%2Boxalate%2Bcomplex%2Bfor%2Blithium-ion%2Bbatteries%26doi%3D10.1016%252Fj.electacta.2015.08.109&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.7b16402&amp;doiOfLink=10.1016%2Fj.electacta.2015.08.109&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit30R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">30</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Porous spherical LiMnPO4·2Li3V2(PO4)3/C cathode material synthesized via spray-drying route using oxalate complex for lithium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Jia-feng; Wang, Xiao-wei; Zhang, Bao; Tong, Hui</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Electrochimica Acta</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">180</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">507-513</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ELCAAV</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0013-4686</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Porous spherical LiMnPO4·2Li3V2(PO4)3/C composite was synthesized innovatively via spray-drying route using oxalate complex.  X-ray diffraction patterns and energy dispersive x-ray results revealed that the composite was composed of LiMnPO4 and Li3V2(PO4)3.  SEM results revealed the porous spherical structure, and TEM results exhibited that the surface of the microsphere was coated with C layer of ∼5.1 nm thickness.  The mutual doping phenomenon between LiMnPO4 and Li3V2(PO4)3 was also confirmed by high resoln. TEM and Fourier transform observation.  Porous spherical LiMnPO4·2Li3V2(PO4)3/C delivered an initial capacity of 132.6 mAh g-1 at 0.1 C and noticeably enhanced high rate capacities at 1, 3 and 10 C.  Compared with solid spherical LiMnPO4·2Li3V2(PO4)3/C, cycle performance, high-rate performance and Li ion intercalation performance of porous spherical LiMnPO4·2Li3V2(PO4)3/C were all significantly improved.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li></ol></div><script type="text/javascript" nonce="931887ddac8454b8-SJC">window.refViewer={'ref1':['cit1'],'ref2':['cit2'],'ref3':['cit3'],'ref4':['cit4'],'ref5':['cit5'],'ref6':['cit6'],'ref7':['cit7'],'ref8':['cit8'],'ref9':['cit9'],'ref10':['cit10'],'ref11':['cit11'],'ref12':['cit12'],'ref13':['cit13'],'ref14':['cit14'],'ref15':['cit15'],'ref16':['cit16'],'ref17':['cit17'],'ref18':['cit18'],'ref19':['cit19'],'ref20':['cit20'],'ref21':['cit21'],'ref22':['cit22'],'ref23':['cit23'],'ref24':['cit24'],'ref25':['cit25'],'ref26':['cit26'],'ref27':['cit27'],'ref28':['cit28'],'ref29':['cit29'],'ref30':['cit30']}</script><div class="articleCitedByDropzone" data-pb-dropzone="articleCitedByDropzone"><div class="cited-by"><div class="article_content-header cited-content_header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div tabindex="0" class="article_content-title"><h2 id="citeThis">Cited By</h2><div class="article__copy"> <button class="article__copy__btn"><i aria-hidden="true" class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><div class="cited-by__content"><div class="sciteMetricsDropzone">

                        rightTab-cas_cit2R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">2</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Quantitative Structure-Activity Relationship (QSAR) for the Oxidation of Trace Organic Contaminants by Sulfate Radical</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Xiao, Ruiyang; Ye, Tiantian; Wei, Zongsu; Luo, Shuang; Yang, Zhihui; Spinney, Richard</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Environmental Science &amp; Technology</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">49</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">22</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">13394-13402</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ESTHAG</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0013-936X</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The sulfate radical anion (SO4•-) based oxidn. of trace org. contaminants (TrOCs) has recently received great attention due to its high reactivity and low selectivity.  In this study, a meta-anal. was conducted to better understand the role of functional groups on the reactivity between SO4•- and TrOCs.  The results indicate that compds. in which electron transfer and addn. channels dominate tend to exhibit a faster second-order rate consts. (kSO•-4) than that of H-atom abstraction, corroborating the SO4•- reactivity and mechanisms obsd. in the individual studies.  Then, a quant. structure activity relationship (QSAR) model was developed using a sequential approach with constitutional, geometrical, electrostatic, and quantum chem. descriptors.  Two descriptors, ELUMO and EHOMO energy gap (ELUMO-EHOMO) and the ratio of oxygen atoms to carbon atoms (#O:C), were found to mechanistically and statistically affect kSO•-4 to a great extent with the standardized QSAR model: ln kSO•-4 = 26.8-3.97 × #O:C - 0.746 × (ELUMO-EHOMO).  In addn., the correlation anal. indicates that there is no dominant reaction channel for SO4•- reactions with various structurally diverse compds.  Our QSAR model provides a robust predictive tool for estg. emerging micropollutants removal using SO4•- during wastewater treatment processes.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref3"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref3" class="rightTabRefNumLink">3</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit3" data-doi="10.1021/acs.est.5b03744"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xiao, R.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zammit, I.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wei, Z.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Hu, W. P.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">MacLeod, M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Spinney, R.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Kinetics and Mechanism of the Oxidation of Cyclic Methylsiloxanes by Hydroxyl Radical in the Gas Phase: An Experimental and Theoretical Study</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Environ. Sci. Technol.</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2015</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">49</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">13322</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">13330</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1021/acs.est.5b03744</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit3R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">3</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Kinetics and Mechanism of the Oxidation of Cyclic Methylsiloxanes by Hydroxyl Radical in the Gas Phase: An Experimental and Theoretical Study</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Xiao, Ruiyang; Zammit, Ian; Wei, Zongsu; Hu, Wei-Ping; MacLeod, Matthew; Spinney, Richard</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Environmental Science &amp; Technology</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">49</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">22</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">13322-13330</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ESTHAG</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0013-936X</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The ubiquitous presence of cyclic volatile methylsiloxanes (cVMS) in the global atm. has recently raised environmental concern.  In order to assess the persistence and long-range transport potential of cVMS, their second-order rate consts. (k) for reactions with hydroxyl radical (•OH) in the gas phase are needed.  We exptl. and theor. investigated the kinetics and mechanism of •OH oxidn. of a series of cVMS, hexamethylcyclotrisiloxane (D3), octamethylcyclotetrasiloxane (D4), and decamethycyclopentasiloxane (D5).  Exptl., we measured k values for D3, D4, and D5 with •OH in a gas-phase reaction chamber.  The Arrhenius activation energies for these reactions in the temp. range from 313 to 353 K were small (-2.92 to 0.79 kcal·mol-1), indicating a weak temp. dependence.  We also calcd. the thermodn. and kinetic behaviors for reactions at the M06-2X/6-311++G**//M06-2X/6-31+G** level of theory over a wider temp. range of 238-358 K that encompasses temps. in the troposphere.  The calcd. Arrhenius activation energies range from -2.71 to -1.64 kcal·mol-1, also exhibiting weak temp. dependence.  The measured k values were approx. an order of magnitude higher than the theor. values but have the same trend with increasing size of the siloxane ring.  The calcd. energy barriers for H-atom abstraction at different positions were similar, which provides theor. support for extrapolating k for other cyclic siloxanes from the no. of abstractable hydrogens.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref4"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref4" class="rightTabRefNumLink">4</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit4" data-doi="10.1016/j.scitotenv.2017.03.039"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yang, Z. Q.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xiao, R. Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wei, Z.         </div><div class="casAbstract">The morphol. optimization of Na3V2(PO4)3 (NVP) material has a great significance for improving the electrochem. performance since NVP suffers from intrinsic low electronic cond.  For this purpose, a novel 3D NVP nanofiber network is controllably constructed via a facile self-sacrificed template method.  Based on time-dependent expts., an outside-in morphol. evolution mechanism from microsphere to 3D nanofiber network is proposed.  The as-synthesized material exhibits excellent cyclability (95.9% capacity retention over 1000 cycles at 10 C) and enhanced high-rate performance (94 mA h g-1 at 100 C) for sodium half cell. Such remarkable performance is attributed to the 3D nanofiber network structure, which provides multi-channel ionic diffusion pathway, continuous electronic conduction, and improved structural integrity.         </div><div class="casAbstract">The energy crisis and energy security leads a great attention to Li-ion batteries (LIB) as the excellent power candidates.  The authors successfully synthesized LiMnPO4·Li3V2(PO4)3/C composite cathode material with high capacity and excellent cycling performance from prickly MnV2O6·2H2O precursor, following chem. redn. and lithiation with double C sources.  The LiMnPO4·Li3V2(PO4)3/C sample has a special multicore-shell structure, whose inner stuffing are LiMnPO4 and Li3V2(PO4)3 at 5-25 nm.  The initial discharge capacity of LiMnPO4·Li3V2(PO4)3/C composite delivers 221.4 mAh g-1, 202.3 mAh g-1 and 152.9 mAh g-1 at the rate of 0.1 C, 1 C and 5 C at 1.5-4.5 V, and retains 99.5%, 99.1% and 94.3% of its initial discharge capacity after 50 cycles, resp.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref28"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref28" class="rightTabRefNumLink">28</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit28" data-doi="10.1016/j.jpowsour.2016.02.066"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Klee, R.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Lavela, P.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Aragon, M. J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Alcantara, R.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Tirado, J. L.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Enhanced high-rate performance of manganese substituted Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub>/C as cathode for sodium-ion batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">J. Power Sources</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2016</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">313</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">73</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">80</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1016/j.jpowsour.2016.02.066</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit28R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">28</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Enhanced high-rate performance of manganese substituted Na3V2(PO4)3/C as cathode for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Klee, R.; Lavela, P.; Aragon, M. J.; Alcantara, R.; Tirado, J. L.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Power Sources</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">313</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">73-80</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JPSODZ</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0378-7753</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Composites with general stoichiometry Na3V2-xMnx(PO4)3/C (0 ≤ x ≤ 0.7) have been evaluated as cathode materials in sodium-ion batteries.  The sol-gel method here employed favors the formation of a homogeneously dispersed carbon conductive phase.  XRD patterns show a limited soly. of Mn in the NASICON structure.  The substitution of 0.3-0.5 manganese per formula unit promotes the formation of a homogeneous composite.  XPS spectra evidence an effective substitution of V3+ by Mn3+.  Galvanostatic cycling of sodium half-cell reveal a plateau at 3.4 V ascribable to the V4+/V3+ redox couple.  A small and reversible plateau at ca. 3.85 V is also obsd. for x ≥ 0.3, and ascribed to the activation of the V5+/V4+ redox couple, according to XPS spectroscopy.  Ex-situ XRD patterns NayV1.7Mn0.3(PO4)3 evidence the occurrence of a reversible two phase mechanism of sodium insertion.  An optimized performance is achieved for Na3V1.7Mn0.3(PO4)3/C, reaching a capacity value of 104 mA h/g at C/2 and 92 mA h/g at 2C.  It is ascribed to the optimal morphol., leading to low internal resistance and favorable electrode-electrolyte interphase.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref29"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref29" class="rightTabRefNumLink">29</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit29" data-doi="10.1016/j.jpowsour.2013.03.035"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Shu, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wu, Q.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Hu, B.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yang, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wei, Q.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liang, Q.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Bai, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhou, M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wu, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chen, M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, A.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Jiang, L.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Improved electrochemical performance of LiFePO<sub>4</sub>/C cathode via Ni and Mn co-doping for lithium-ion batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">J. Power Sources</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2013</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">237</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">149</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">155</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1016/j.jpowsour.2013.03.035</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit29R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">29</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Improved electrochemical performance of LiFePO4/C cathode via Ni and Mn co-doping for lithium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Shu, Hongbo; Wang, Xianyou; Wu, Qiang; Hu, Benan; Yang, Xiukang; Wei, Qiliang; Liang, Qianqian; Bai, Yansong; Zhou, Meng; Wu, Chun; Chen, Manfang; Wang, Aiwen; Jiang, Lanlan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Power Sources</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2013</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">237</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">149-155</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JPSODZ</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0378-7753</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The pristine LiFePO4/C and Ni and Mn co-doped LiFe1-x-yNixMnyPO4/C (x = 0.01-0.04; y = 0.04-0.01) composites are synthesized by a simple high-temp. solid-state route.  The structure, morphol. and electrochem. performance of the samples are characterized by x-ray diffraction, FTIR spectra, SEM, charge/discharge tests and electrochem. impedance spectroscopy.  The results indicate that the Ni and Mn co-doping does not destroy the olivine structure of LiFePO4, but it can stabilize the crystal structure, lengthen the Li-O bond, decrease charge transfer resistance, enhance Li ion diffusion velocity, and thus improve the cycling and high-rate capability of the LiFePO4/C.  Esp., the LiFe0.95Ni0.02Mn0.03PO4/C shows the best cycling stability and rate capability among all the doped samples.  The first discharge capacity of LiFe0.95Ni0.02Mn0.03PO4/C is 145.4 mA-h/g with the capacity retention ratio of 98.6% for 100 cycles at 1C.  Even at a high rate of 10C, it still shows a high discharge capacity of 115.2 mA-h/g.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref30"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref30" class="rightTabRefNumLink">30</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit30" data-doi="10.1016/j.electacta.2015.08.109"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhang, J.-f.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, X.-w.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhang, B.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Tong, H.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Porous spherical LiMnPO<sub>4</sub>·2Li<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub>/C cathode material synthesized via spray-drying route using oxalate complex for lithium-ion batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Electrochim. Acta</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2015</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">180</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">507</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">513</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1016/j.electacta.2015.08.109</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit30R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">30</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Porous spherical LiMnPO4·2Li3V2(PO4)3/C cathode material synthesized via spray-drying route using oxalate complex for lithium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Jia-feng; Wang, Xiao-wei; Zhang, Bao; Tong, Hui</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Electrochimica Acta</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">180</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">507-513</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ELCAAV</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0013-4686</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Porous spherical LiMnPO4·2Li3V2(PO4)3/C composite was synthesized innovatively via spray-drying route using oxalate complex.  X-ray diffraction patterns and energy dispersive x-ray results revealed that the composite was composed of LiMnPO4 and Li3V2(PO4)3.  SEM results revealed the porous spherical structure, and TEM results exhibited that the surface of the microsphere was coated with C layer of ∼5.1 nm thickness.  The mutual doping phenomenon between LiMnPO4 and Li3V2(PO4)3 was also confirmed by high resoln. TEM and Fourier transform observation.  Porous spherical LiMnPO4·2Li3V2(PO4)3/C delivered an initial capacity of 132.6 mAh g-1 at 0.1 C and noticeably enhanced high rate capacities at 1, 3 and 10 C.  Compared with solid spherical LiMnPO4·2Li3V2(PO4)3/C, cycle performance, high-rate performance and Li ion intercalation performance of porous spherical LiMnPO4·2Li3V2(PO4)3/C were all significantly improved.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li></ol></li></ul></div></div></div></div></article><div class="w-slide article__w-slide">

(function(){
	
	/*Event Tracking for RIS menu dropdown - Article pages*/

	$('.cit-download-dropdown_button').on('click',function(e)
	{	
		e.preventDefault();
	    gtag('event', 'Export', { 'event_category': 'Citation', 'event_label':'Main'});

	});


	$('.cit-download-dropdown_content ul li').on('click',function(e)
	{	
	//	e.preventDefault();
	    var idx = $(this).index();
	    
	    var label = '';
	    if (idx === 0 ) {
	    	label = 'Citation';
	    } else if (idx === 1 ) {
	    	label = 'Abstract';
	    } else if (idx === 2 ) {
	    	label = 'Reference';
	    } else if (idx === 3 ) {
	    	label = 'More Options';
	    }
	   
	   gtag('event', 'Export', { 'event_category': 'Citation', 'event_label':label});
	});

	$('.header_contnav-next a').on('click', function(e){
        e.preventDefault();
        gtag('event', 'Top', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Right Arrow'});
	}); 

 	$('.header_contnav-pre a').on('click', function(e){
	    e.preventDefault();
	     gtag('event', 'Top', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Left Arrow'});
	}); 

	$('.share_button').on('click', function(e){
		e.preventDefault();
		gtag('event', 'Top', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Share'});
	});

	$("#pane-m1con").on('click', function(e) {
		e.preventDefault();
		gtag('event', 'Sidebar', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Figures'});
	});

	$("#pane-m2con").on('click', function(e) {
		e.preventDefault();
	    gtag('event', 'Sidebar', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'References'});
	});

	$("#pane-m3con").on('click', function(e) {
		e.preventDefault();
		gtag('event', 'Sidebar', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Supporting Info'});
	});

	$('.tab__close').on('click', function(){
		gtag('event', 'Sidebar', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Close'});
	}); 



})();

</script>

<script nonce="931887ddac8454b8-SJC">
document.addEventListener('DOMContentLoaded', function () {
    const modalContainer = document.querySelector('.my-main-container');

    // Function to show the modal
    function showModal() {
        modalContainer.style.display = 'flex';
        document.querySelector('.overlay').style.display = 'block';
    }

    // Function to hide the modal when the close button is clicked
    function hideModal() {
        modalContainer.style.display = 'none';
        document.querySelector('.overlay').style.display = 'none';
    }

    // Hide the modal initially
    hideModal();

    // Function to handle clicks outside the modal
    function handleClickOutside(event) {
        // const modalContainer = document.querySelector(".my-main-container");
        // Check if the click target is not a child of the modal container
        if (!modalContainer.contains(event.target)) {
            hideModal();
        }
    }

    // Add a click event listener to the close button
    document
        .querySelector('.close-button')
        .addEventListener('click', hideModal);

    // Add a click event listener to the document to handle clicks outside the modal
    document.addEventListener('click', handleClickOutside);

    const screenHeight = window.innerHeight;
    function updateModalPosition() {
        const scrollY = window.scrollY;
        // console.log("scrollY= " + scrollY);
        // modalContainer.style.top = `${50 + scrollY}px`;
        modalContainer.style.top = `${scrollY + screenHeight / 2}px`;
        // console.log("new top= " + modalContainer.style.top);
    }

    // Update the modal position when the user scrolls
    window.addEventListener('scroll', updateModalPosition);

    // Initialize the modal position
    updateModalPosition();

    //---Cookie---
    // Function to set the cookie with a given name, value, and expiration time in days
    function setCookie(name, value, days) {
        var expires = '';
        if (days) {
            var date = new Date();
            date.setTime(date.getTime() + days * 24 * 60 * 60 * 1000);
            expires = '; expires=' + date.toUTCString();
            console.log(expires + 'this is expires dateUTC');
        }
        document.cookie = name + '=' + (value || '') + expires + '; path=/';
        // console.log("document.cookie is: " + document.cookie);
    }

    if (!document.cookie.includes('modalAd')) {
        // Show Modal
        showModal();

        // Set the cookie with the name "modalAd", value "true", and expiration of 3 day
        setCookie('modalAd', 'true', 3);
    } else {
        hideModal();
    }
});

</script>

<script nonce="931887ddac8454b8-SJC">
    document.addEventListener("DOMContentLoaded", function(){
    // Function to get a Human readable formatted date
    function getFormattedDateForMaintenance() {
        let today = new Date();
        let dd = String(today.getDate()).padStart(2, '0');
        //January is 0
        let mm = String(today.getMonth() + 1).padStart(2, '0'); 
        let yyyy = today.getFullYear();
        
        let daysOfWeek = ['Sunday', 'Monday', 'Tuesday', 'Wednesday', 'Thursday', 'Friday', 'Saturday'];
        let monthsOfYear = ['January', 'February', 'March', 'April', 'May', 'June', 'July', 'August', 'September', 'October', 'November', 'December'];

        let dayOfWeek = daysOfWeek[today.getDay()];
        let monthOfYear = monthsOfYear[today.getMonth()];

        return dayOfWeek + ', ' + monthOfYear + ' ' + dd + ', ' + yyyy;
    }
    
    // Insert the date into the .system-message-date element
    document.querySelector('.system-message-date').innerText = getFormattedDateForMaintenance();
});
</script>

        var check = false;
        (function (a) {
          if (
            /(android|bb\d+|meego).+mobile|avantgo|bada\/|blackberry|blazer|compal|elaine|fennec|hiptop|iemobile|ip(hone|od)|iris|kindle|lge |maemo|midp|mmp|mobile.+firefox|netfront|opera m(ob|in)i|palm( os)?|phone|p(ixi|re)\/|plucker|pocket|psp|series(4|6)0|symbian|treo|up\.(browser|link)|vodafone|wap|windows ce|xda|xiino/i.test(

      var emailValid = "",
        time = 3000,
        btnStatus = true,
        errorStatus = false,
        errormessage =
          "<p class='gdpr_err'><b>Please Enter a valid email address<b><p>";

      function init() {
        setTimeout(function () {
          var cookieExist = getCookie("gdpr");
          if (cookieExist) {
            //console.log("gdpr cookie exist");
            return false;
          } else {
            //console.log("gdpr cookie does not exist")
            gdprMessage();
          }
          //Events
          $("#closebtn").on("click", hideForm);

          //Handle submit
          $("#gdpr-message-btn").on("click", function (event) {
            handleClick();
          });

          // //Hide if clicked outside div - TO DO stop handling click after submit
          // $(document).click(function(event) {
          // 	event.stopPropagation();
          //   console.log(event.target);
          //   if (!$(event.target).closest("#gdpr-message-content").length) {
          //     $("body").find("#gdpr-message-modal").hide();
          //     $(this).off();
          //   }
          // });
          $("#gdpr-con-btn").click(function () {
            setCookie("gdpr", "true");
            hideForm();
          });
        }, time);
      }

      //Show the message
      function gdprMessage() {
        //console.log("Show GDPR Message");
        var tMessage, emailInput, messageButton, ewrap;

        $("#gdpr-message-modal").show();
      }

      function handleClick() {
        //console.log($("#gdpr-input").val());
        emailValid = validateEmail($("#gdpr-input").val());
        if (emailValid) {
          //Submit the form
          //Hide form
          if ($(".gdpr_err")) {
            $(".gdpr_err").hide();
          }

          $("#gdpr-message-content");
          //If successful then...
          setCookie("gdpr", "true");
          //console.log("emailValid " + emailValid + " submiting form");
        } else {
          //Show error message
          gdprErrorMessage();
          //console.log("emailValid " + emailValid);
        }
      }

      function gdprErrorMessage() {
        if (errorStatus) {
          return false;
        } else {
          errorStatus = true;
          $("#gdpr-message-content").append(errormessage);
        }
      }

      function validateEmail(email) {
        var re =
          /^(([^<>()\[\]\\.,;:\s@"]+(\.[^<>()\[\]\\.,;:\s@"]+)*)|(".+"))@((\[[0-9]{1,3}\.[0-9]{1,3}\.[0-9]{1,3}\.[0-9]{1,3}\])|(([a-zA-Z\-0-9]+\.)+[a-zA-Z]{2,}))$/;
        return re.test(String(email).toLowerCase());
      }

      function setCookie(name, value) {
        var expires = "";
        expires = "; expires=Fri, 31 Dec 9999 23:59:59 GMT";
        document.cookie = name + "=" + (value || "") + expires + "; path=/";
      }

      function getCookie(name) {
        var match = document.cookie.match(new RegExp(name + "=([^;]+)"));
        if (match) return match[1];
      }

      function hideForm() {
        //And set cookie
        $("#gdpr-message-modal").hide();
        setCookie("gdpr", "false");
        gtag("event", "GDPR Modal", {
          event_category: "Pubs GDPR",
          event_label: "GDPR Dismissal",
        });
      }

      return {
        init: init,
      };
    })();

    $(document).ready(infoCentralCapture.init);
  </script>
</p>

var currentJournal = "ACS Applied Materials &amp;amp; Interfaces";
$(".citationLinks > a").click(function(e){
    if($(this).text() === "ACS Full Text ") {
        gtag('event', 'ACS Full Text', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).text() === "Crossref") {
        gtag('event', 'Crossref', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).text() === "CAS") {
        gtag('event', 'CAS', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).text() === "PubMed") {
        gtag('event', 'PubMed', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).text() === "Google Scholar") {
        gtag('event', 'Google Scholar', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).hasClass("issue-item_open-url") === true) {
        gtag('event', 'OpenURL', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
});
</script>
